compact, affordable and capable","link":"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/field-review-panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-asph-compact-affordable-and-capable","description":"<h2>Introduction</h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-6.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"443\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S590x0~articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-6.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-6.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S1180x0~articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-6.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<div class=\"rightFloatedBox\">\n <a class=\"articleProductBadgeAndScore\" href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/field-review-panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-asph#conclusion\"><span class=\"badge\"><img src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/resources/images/award-gold-dark.png?v=5310\" alt=\"Gold Award\" title=\"Gold Award\" /></span>\n  <div class=\"scoreContainer\">\n   <div class=\"score\">\n    83%\n   </div>\n   <div class=\"scoreTip\">\n    Overall score\n   </div>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"link\">\n   Jump to conclusion\n   <span class=\"caret\"></span>\n  </div></a>\n</div> \n<p>The Panasonic Lumix G 25mm F1.7 ASPH is a compact and lightweight prime lens for Micro Four Thirds camera bodies. It offers an equivalent focal length of 50mm in full-frame terms, and an <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/learn/2799100497/equivalence-in-a-nutshell\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">equivalent maximum aperture</a> of F3.4. This lens is a great choice for general-purpose photography, including low-light work.</p> \n<p>At $250 USD and available now, the Lumix G 25mm F1.7 is a solid option whether you're looking for a companion to your 'kit' zoom lens or you just want something small and fast to shoot with.</p> \n<hr> \n <p class=\"newsLink\" id=\"top\">Jump to:</p> \n <p class=\"newsLink\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/field-review-panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-asph-compact-affordable-and-capable#handling\">Handling </a>| <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/field-review-panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-asph-compact-affordable-and-capable#compare\">Compared to</a> |<a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/field-review-panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-asph-compact-affordable-and-capable#autofocus\">Autofocus and focus breathing </a>| <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/field-review-panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-asph-compact-affordable-and-capable#imagequality\">Image quality</a> | <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/field-review-panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-asph-compact-affordable-and-capable#conclusion\">Conclusion </a>| <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/field-review-panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-asph-compact-affordable-and-capable#samplegalleries\">Samples</a> | <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/field-review-panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-asph/2\">Full specifications</a></p> \n <hr> \n  <h3>Key specifications:</h3> \n  <ul> \n   <li><strong>Focal length:</strong> 25mm (50mm Full-Frame equivalent)</li> \n   <li><strong>Aperture range:</strong> F1.7 – 22</li> \n   <li><strong>Stabilization:</strong> None built-in</li> \n   <li><strong>Filter thread:</strong> 46mm</li> \n   <li><strong>Close focus:</strong> 0.25 m (9.84″)</li> \n   <li><strong>Maximum magnification:</strong> 0.14x</li> \n   <li><strong>Diaphragm blades:</strong> seven</li> \n   <li><strong>Hood:</strong> yes (plastic, included)</li> \n   <li><strong>Weight:</strong> 125 g (0.28 lb)</li> \n   <li><strong>Optical construction: </strong>8 elements in 7 groups</li> \n  </ul> \n  <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n   <tbody> \n    <tr> \n     <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/Samples/3050744648.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"443\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/3050744648.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Samples/3050744648.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/3050744648.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n    </tr> \n    <tr> \n     <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">ISO 200 | 1/800 sec | F4 | Panasonic Lumix DC-G9</td> \n    </tr> \n   </tbody> \n  </table> \n  <p>Ah, the nifty fifty. Back in the film camera days, long before the advent of the zooming kit lens, camera companies often shipped their consumer and enthusiast bodies kitted with a 50mm lens; a practice I'd be thrilled to see come back. After all, they say you become a better photographer, <em>faster</em>, 'zooming' with your feet rather than zooming with your lens. Why? Because moving around forces creativity and often opens up new perspectives!</p> \n  <p>Anyhow, the hallmark of any good nifty fifty, then and now, is a favorable ratio of quality to price. And Panasonic's modern take for Micro Four Thirds fits the bill nicely: though it's very affordable, it's capable of producing lovely images.</p> \n  <p>Follow along as we jump into handling, AF behavior, and optical characteristics to find out if this lens is also a good choice for you.</p> \n  <p><em>Sample images in this review were edited in Adobe Camera Raw with adjustments limited to white balance and exposure parameters. Sharpening and noise reduction were left at ACR defaults.</em></p> \n  <p><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/field-review-panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-asph-compact-affordable-and-capable#top\"><strong>Back to top</strong></a></p> \n  <hr> \n   <h2 id=\"handling\">Handling</h2> \n   <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n    <tbody> \n     <tr> \n      <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-4.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"443\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-4.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-4.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-4.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n     </tr> \n    </tbody> \n   </table> \n   <p>At 125g (4.4 oz) in weight and just 52mm (2 in) in length, this 25mm F1.7 is among Panasonic's smallest and lightest prime lenses. The mount is metal while the body is constructed of plastic. Despite the delightfully lightweight design, it looks and feels well-built.</p> \n   <p>As one should expect at the price point, this 25mm offers a bare-bones feature-set. There's no optical stabilization, though this shouldn't matter for the vast majority of shooters, as almost all modern Micro Four Thirds bodies have internal IS. Nor is there an aperture ring or custom buttons. What the lens does offer is a sizable focus ring.</p> \n   <p>The front accepts 46mm filters and a plastic lens hood, H-H025, is included in the box. The hood attaches bayonet style, so it can be used with a filter. It can also be attached backward, to save space.</p> \n   <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop twoBottom center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"250\"> \n    <tbody> \n     <tr> \n      <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 250px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-2.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"250\" height=\"188\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS250x0~articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-2.jpeg\" width=\"250\" data-filename=\"product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-2.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS500x0~articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-2.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n      <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 250px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-3.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"250\" height=\"188\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS250x0~articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-3.jpeg\" width=\"250\" data-filename=\"product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-3.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS500x0~articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-3.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n     </tr> \n    </tbody> \n   </table> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/field-review-panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-asph-compact-affordable-and-capable#top\"><strong>Back to top</strong></a></p> \n   <hr> \n    <h2 id=\"compare\">Compared to...</h2> \n    <p>Olympus also makes a 'nifty fifty' similar to this one. It's a little more expensive, but it's also a bit more compact. Other options in this segment include the faster, though longer Sigma 30mm F1.4 and the higher-end Panasonic/Leica 25mm F1.4 II.</p> \n    <p>Here's how they all stack up:</p> \n    <div href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/field-review-panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-asph-compact-affordable-and-capable#top\"><strong>Back to top</strong></a></p> \n    <hr> \n     <h2 id=\"autofocus\">Autofocus and focus breathing</h2> \n     <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n      <tbody> \n       <tr> \n        <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-5.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"443\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-5.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-5.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-5.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n       </tr> \n      </tbody> \n     </table> \n     <p>The Panasonic 25mm F1.7 is plenty fast to focus on a Lumix body; and shooting in AF-S tends to lead to faster AF acquisition than using AF-C. The lens is also snappy to focus with Olympus bodies, though given how close in price the Olympus 25mm F1.8 is to this lens, we'd recommend sticking with the native option for best AF performance.</p> \n     <p>The minimum focus distance of 0.25m or just shy of 10 inches is solid. Users will be able to get fairly up-close and personal with their subjects. And focusing is internal, meaning the lens does not increase in size as it racks.</p> \n     <div class=\"beer-slider-container\">\n      <div id=\"slider2\" class=\"beer-slider\" data-beer-label=\"Focused at infinity\">\n       <img src=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/Lumix-G-25mm-slide-2.jpeg\">\n        <div class=\"beer-reveal\" data-beer-label=\"Focused at ~2ft\">\n         <img src=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/Lumix-G-25mm-slide-1.jpeg\" />\n        </div></img>\n      </div>\n     </div> \n     <p>For video shooters, focus breathing – where the framing shifts as the focus is pulled – is fairly well controlled. This is good news for folks who may want to manually rack focus for a cinematic effect. The manual focus action is a focus-by-wire affair and responsive enough; the ring itself turns with no hard stop at either end of the focus range.</p> \n     <p>The lens is also impressively quiet when using AF in video mode thanks to its stepper motor. We tested it with a Panasonic G9 and found the touchscreen makes it painless to move focus smoothly and silently, with just the tap of a finger.</p> \n     <p><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/field-review-panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-asph-compact-affordable-and-capable#top\"><strong>Back to top</strong></a></p> \n     <hr> \n      <h2 id=\"imagequality\">Image quality</h2> \n      <h3>Sharpness</h3> \n      <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n       <tbody> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044279.acr.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"442\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S590x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044279.acr.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Samples/P1044279.acr.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S1180x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044279.acr.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n        </tr> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">ISO 200 | 1/4000 sec | F1.7 | Panasonic Lumix G9</td> \n        </tr> \n       </tbody> \n      </table> \n      <p>This Panasonic 25mm F1.7 is fairly sharp across the focal plane, wide open. And even on the highest resolution 20MP Four Thirds sensors, its resolving power should leave most users satisfied.</p> \n      <p>That being said, stopping down just a bit to <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/sample-galleries/1927835807/panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-sample-gallery/1558392485\">F2 or F2.8</a> will result in the sharpest output. But sharpness will drop quite visibly by even F5.6 and certainly by F8, due to diffraction (remembering that F5.6 - F8 on Four Thirds is F11 - F22 in full-frame terms). So it's better to crank your shutter speed in bright light, rather than go beyond those apertures, if possible.</p> \n      <h3>Vignetting and distortion</h3> \n      <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n       <tbody> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044332.acr.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"442\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044332.acr.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Samples/P1044332.acr.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044332.acr.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n        </tr> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\"> <p>This lens displays minimal vignetting wide open. And any noticeable vignetting is gone by F2.8.</p> <p>ISO 200 | 1/1250 sec | F2.8 | Panasonic Lumix G9</p> </td> \n        </tr> \n       </tbody> \n      </table> \n      <p>While the lens has a fair degree of <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/sample-galleries/1927835807/panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-sample-gallery/2325774983\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">barrel distortion</a> in its optical design (which is to be expected, as the M43 system prioritizes compact size), distortion is fully corrected for, digitally, in the camera's JPEGs and/or in your Raw converter. This means straight lines will look, well, straight (see the images above the flowers for an example). The lens also shows <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/sample-galleries/1927835807/panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-sample-gallery/5128249301\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">minimal vignetting wide open</a> and any traces of vignetting are <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/sample-galleries/1927835807/panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-sample-gallery/4801537171\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">gone by F2.8</a>.</p> \n      <p>If the tiny bit of vignetting does bother you, it can easily be corrected for in post. I personally enjoy it, though, as a matter of taste. But to each their own!</p> \n      <h3>Bokeh</h3> \n      <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n       <tbody> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044358.acr.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"442\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S590x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044358.acr.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Samples/P1044358.acr.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S1180x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044358.acr.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n        </tr> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">ISO 200 | 1/2000 sec | F1.7 | Panasonic Lumix G9</td> \n        </tr> \n       </tbody> \n      </table> \n      <p>The bokeh – or quality of the out-of-focus regions produced by this 25mm – is fairly pleasing. Panasonic takes pride in the smoothness/polishing of its aspherical surfaces/molds, and it shows here. The discs rendered by out-of-focus highlights are relatively Gaussian and free of distracting patterns like 'onion rings'. Only occasionally do they show the slightest hint of a hard edge (more noticeable as you <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/sample-galleries/1927835807/panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-sample-gallery/6341729838\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">stop down</a>), but not enough to cause any concern.</p> \n      <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop twoBottom center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"250\"> \n       <tbody> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 250px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044363.acr.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"250\" height=\"188\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS250x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044363.acr.jpeg\" width=\"250\" data-filename=\"Samples/P1044363.acr.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS500x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044363.acr.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n         <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 250px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044373.acr.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"250\" height=\"188\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS250x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044373.acr.jpeg\" width=\"250\" data-filename=\"Samples/P1044373.acr.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS500x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044373.acr.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n        </tr> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 250px;\">At F1.7, bokeh near the edge of the frame displays a 'cat eye' effect.</td> \n         <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 250px;\">At F4, bokeh looks much more uniform, in terms of its shape.</td> \n        </tr> \n       </tbody> \n      </table> \n      <p>However, when shooting wide open, bokeh near the edge of the frame looks lopsided, displaying the classic 'cat eye' effect. While this can lead to a <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/sample-galleries/1927835807/panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-sample-gallery/8412553300\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">slightly less shallow DOF effect at edges</a>, it's perfectly acceptable for a lens of this type, and wasn't severe enough to yield swirly bokeh in our shots. More importantly, the discs near the corners aren't truncated in an odd or distracting manner.</p> \n      <p>The 'cats-eye' bokeh is mostly gone by F4. However, bokeh discs becomes less rounded. Specifically, the polygonal shape of the lens's 7-blade aperture becomes more pronounced in the out-of-focus highlights, when you stop down past F2.8, and this can have a slightly negative impact on bokeh in general.</p> \n      <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n       <tbody> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/Samples/8866514218.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"443\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S590x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/8866514218.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Samples/8866514218.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S1180x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/8866514218.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n        </tr> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\"> <p>The Panasonic 25mm F1.7 is capable of producing images with good subject separation from the background.</p> <p>ISO 200 | 1/3200 sec | F2.2 | Panasonic Lumix G9</p> </td> \n        </tr> \n       </tbody> \n      </table> \n      <h3>Flaring, ghosting, and sunstars</h3> \n      <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n       <tbody> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044222.acr.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"442\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S590x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044222.acr.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Samples/P1044222.acr.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S1180x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044222.acr.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n        </tr> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\"> <p>Lens flare can cause some loss of contrast especially when shooting directly into bright light sources, while multiple ghosts of bright sources can manifest themselves as colored 'blobs' that get more defined the more you stop the lens down.</p> <p>ISO 200 | 1/800 sec | F16 | Panasonic Lumix G9</p> </td> \n        </tr> \n       </tbody> \n      </table> \n      <p>Even when shooting with the included lens hood attached, artifacts from lens flare can be pretty distracting with this lens. You may notice ghosting when shooting directly into the sun, usually manifesting as a multiple-color haze or purple blobs.</p> \n      <p>When shooting bright light sources at stopped-down apertures – like in the F16 shot above – the 'spikes' of the sunstar are soft-edged and not all that well pronounced.</p> \n      <h3>Lateral and longitudinal chromatic aberration (fringing)</h3> \n      <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n       <tbody> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/0248363764.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"442\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/3264890176/0248363764.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"0248363764.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/3264890176/0248363764.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n        </tr> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\"> <p>The out-of-focus regions in this F1.7 shot show some purple fringing in front of the subject, aka longitudinal CA (LoCA)</p> <p>ISO 200 | 1/3200 sec | F1.7 | Panasonic Lumix G9</p> </td> \n        </tr> \n       </tbody> \n      </table> \n      <p>Lateral chromatic aberration – or purple/green fringing near the edge of the frame in high contrast regions – is very well controlled for optically, and is further corrected for digitally in JPEGs and/or in your Raw converter. Here are <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/sample-galleries/1927835807/panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-sample-gallery/1014136621\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">uncorrected</a> and <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/sample-galleries/1927835807/panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-sample-gallery/3038573512\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">corrected</a> Raw conversions - as you can see the differences are minor.</p> \n      <p>Longitudinal CA (LoCA) – or purple and green fringing manifesting in front of and behind the plane of focus – can be fairly <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/sample-galleries/1927835807/panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-sample-gallery/0207843981\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">noticeable wide open</a> and is hard to manually correct for. That said, stopping down the lens just a bit helps to mitigate it, and although it <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/sample-galleries/1927835807/panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-sample-gallery/2843111490\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">doesn't entirely disappear even by F2.8</a>, it's not too distracting either.</p> \n      <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n       <tbody> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/Samples/1795778357.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"442\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S590x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/1795778357.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Samples/1795778357.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S1180x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/1795778357.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n        </tr> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\"> <p>While the Panasonic 25mm F1.7 shows some longitudinal CA wide open, it becomes much less noticeable when you stop down a bit. Still, at 100%, you can certainly spot some purple and green fringing in the out-of-focus regions on the left side of this image, in the vines and stems.</p> <p>ISO 200 | 1/2000 sec | F2.8 | Pansonic Lumix G9</p> </td> \n        </tr> \n       </tbody> \n      </table> \n      <p><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/field-review-panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-asph-compact-affordable-and-capable#top\"><strong>Back to top</strong></a></p> \n      <hr> \n       <h2 id=\"conclusion\">Conclusion</h2> \n       <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n        <tbody> \n         <tr> \n          <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-1.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"443\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-1.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-1.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/3264890176/product/Lumix-G-25mm-F1.7-1.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n         </tr> \n        </tbody> \n       </table> \n       <div class=\"contentTable\"> \n        <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"contentTable\"> \n         <tbody> \n          <tr> \n           <th width=\"50%\">What we like</th> \n           <th width=\"50%\">What we don't like</th> \n          </tr> \n          <tr> \n           <td width=\"50%\"> \n            <ul> \n             <li>Reasonably sharp wide open and even sharper stopped down to F2</li> \n             <li>Fast and quiet to focus</li> \n             <li>Minimal distortion</li> \n             <li>Compact, light-weight design</li> \n             <li>Very affordable</li> \n             <li>Included lens hood</li> \n             <li>Metal lens mount</li> \n            </ul> </td> \n           <td width=\"50%\"> \n            <ul> \n             <li>Sunstars could be more pronounced</li> \n             <li>Lots of visible ghosting artifacts in scenes with a bright light source in the frame</li> \n             <li>Longitudinal CA can be distracting wide open</li> \n             <li>No weather-sealing</li> \n            </ul> </td> \n          </tr> \n         </tbody> \n        </table> \n       </div> \n       <p>The Pansonic Lumix G 25mm F1.7 ASPH is an affordable and capable option for Four-Thirds shooters seeking something more versatile than the kit lens, especially for low-light photography. It's well-built, compact, and fast/quiet to focus, making it a good choice for stills and video shooters alike.</p> \n       <p>Of course, for a little more money, you can get Sigma's slightly faster 30mm F1.4 DC DN lens, which is also a <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/sigma-30mm-f1-4-dc-dn-contemporary-micro-four-thirds-lens-review\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">strong optical performer</a>. But the trade-off is a tighter crop (60mm in Full-frame terms) and a lens construction that's quite a bit longer and about twice as heavy as the Panasonic.</p> \n       <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n        <tbody> \n         <tr> \n          <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044239.acr.jpeg\" target=\"article-3264890176\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"443\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S590x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044239.acr.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Samples/P1044239.acr.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S1180x0~articles/3264890176/Samples/P1044239.acr.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n         </tr> \n         <tr> \n          <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">ISO 200 | 1/800 sec | F5.6 | Panasonic Lumix G9</td> \n         </tr> \n        </tbody> \n       </table> \n       <p>For folks desiring the absolute best 50mm equiv. output for Panasonic Micro Four Thirds cameras, the Panasonic Leica DG 25mm F1.4 II is the ticket. However, at nearly three times the cost of the Panasonic 25mm F1.7, it's not the easiest lens to justify. It's even harder to justify given how solidly this more affordable prime performs.</p> \n       <p>Ultimately, though it's not optically perfect, for most folks, the Panasonic Lumix G 25mm F1.7 ASPH is going to be more than good enough.</p> \n       <p><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/field-review-panasonic-lumix-g-25mm-f1-7-asph-compact-affordable-and-capable#top\"><strong>Back to top</strong></a></p> \n       <hr> \n        <h2 id=\"samplegalleries\">Sample gallery</h2> \n        <p>Please do not reproduce any of these images without prior permission (see our <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/misc/termsandconditions\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">copyright page</a>).</p> \n        <div id=\"embeddedSampleGallery_1927835807\" class=\"summary\">\n               The Panasonic Lumix G 25mm F1.7 ASPH is a great choice for Micro Four Thirds shooters – especially those with Panasonic bodies – looking to score a well-priced, Two of the manual prime lenses are for Sony E-mount cameras, while the other two are for Canon EF- and Nikon F-mount cameras.</p> \n<h2><strong>Zenitar 35mm F2</strong></h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0505622637/lens_zenitar_2_35_e_mount.jpeg\" target=\"article-31f44a729e654560ad814907c99a6748\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"442\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S590x0~articles/0505622637/lens_zenitar_2_35_e_mount.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"lens_zenitar_2_35_e_mount.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S1180x0~articles/0505622637/lens_zenitar_2_35_e_mount.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>First up is the Zenitar 35mm F2 lens for Sony E-mount cameras. The lens is constructed of seven elements in five groups, has an aperture range of F2 through F22, uses a nine-blade aperture diaphragm and its minimum focusing distance is 50cm (<sub>20”</sub>). The lens measures in at roughly 6.1cm (2.4”) long, 4.7cm (1.85”) in diameter and weighs 300g (10.6oz).</p> \n<p>The Zenitar 35mm F2 lens is listed for 54,000 rubles (~$730) on Zenit’s main website, but pricing in other regions likely won’t be an exact conversion, so we’ll have to wait to see how much it retails for outside of Russia when it becomes available on Zenit’s other regional websites.</p> \n<h2><strong>Zenitar 50mm F1.5</strong></h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0505622637/lens_zenitar_1_5_50_e_mount.jpeg\" target=\"article-31f44a729e654560ad814907c99a6748\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"442\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S590x0~articles/0505622637/lens_zenitar_1_5_50_e_mount.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"lens_zenitar_1_5_50_e_mount.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S1180x0~articles/0505622637/lens_zenitar_1_5_50_e_mount.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Next up is the <a href=\"https://www.zenit.photo/catalog/lens-zenitar-1-50-50/\">Zenitar 50mm F1.5 lens</a> (<a href=\"https://www.translatetheweb.com/?ref=TVert&amp;from=&amp;to=en&amp;a=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.zenit.photo%2Fcatalog%2Flens-zenitar-1-50-50%2F\">translated</a>) for Sony E-mount cameras. The lens is constructed of seven elements in three groups, has an aperture range of F1.5 thorugh F22, uses a 13-blade aperture diaphragm and has a 70cm (28”) minimum focusing distance. The lens measures in at 6.1cm (2.4”) long, 4.7cm (1.85”) in diameter and weighs roughly 287g (10oz).</p> \n<p>The Zenitar 50mm F1.5 is listed for 56,000 rubles (~$755) on Zenit’s main website, but as noted above, it’s unknown what the MSRP will be outside of Russia until listing go live.</p> \n<h2><strong>Zenitar 60mm F2.8 Macro</strong></h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0505622637/lens_zenitar_c_2_8_60_macro_1.jpeg\" target=\"article-31f44a729e654560ad814907c99a6748\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"471\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/0505622637/lens_zenitar_c_2_8_60_macro_1.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"lens_zenitar_c_2_8_60_macro_1.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0505622637/lens_zenitar_c_2_8_60_macro_1.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Moving away from Sony E-mount glass, the <a href=\"https://www.zenit.photo/catalog/lens-zenitar-2-8-60-macro/\">Zenitar 60mm F2.8 macro lens</a> (<a href=\"https://www.translatetheweb.com/?from=&amp;to=en&amp;dl=en&amp;ref=trb&amp;a=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.zenit.photo%2Fcatalog%2Flens-zenitar-2-8-60-macro%2F\">translated</a>) is available for Canon EF- and Nikon F-mount cameras. It’s constructed of eight elements in seven groups, has an aperture range of F2.8 through F22, uses a six-blade aperture diaphragm and has a minimum focusing distance of just 23cm (9”). The lens measures in at 8.1cm (3.2”) long, 7.6cm (3”) in diameter and weighs 590g (1.3lbs).</p> \n<p>Zenit has it listed for 36,000 rubles (~$485) on its website, but pricing elsewhere will likely vary when listings start popping up in other regions.</p> \n<h2><strong>Selena 58mm F1.9</strong></h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0505622637/lens_selena_1_9_50_n.jpeg\" target=\"article-31f44a729e654560ad814907c99a6748\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"442\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S590x0~articles/0505622637/lens_selena_1_9_50_n.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"lens_selena_1_9_50_n.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S1180x0~articles/0505622637/lens_selena_1_9_50_n.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Next up is the Selena 58mm F1.9 lens for Canon EF- and Nikon F-mount cameras. survive a 41m (135ft) fall. If that sounds a little hard to believe, you don’t just have to take their word for it—Kolari Vision proved it with a video showing the new filter being dropped from a drone.</p>\n<div class=\"video\"><iframe allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"326\" id=\"videoFrame\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/EyypnVrbThc?rel=0&amp;autohide=1&amp;wmode=transparent&amp;enablejsapi=1\" width=\"580\"></iframe></div>\n<p>As you can see at the end of the drop test video, the filter came away from the ten-story fall with little more than a scratch on the surface of the lens. Kolari Vision attributes this durability to the Corning Gorilla Glass it uses to manufacturer the filter. According to Kolari Vision, Corning’s Gorilla Glass is ‘more than two times stronger than Schott B270 glass to direct impacts, and more resistant to scratches for better lens protection, all while also boasting a high internal transmission and lower refractive index than Schott B270 for sharper images.’</p>\n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop incredibly transparent with over 99% transmission and low reflection while cutting UV at 415nm, a strong cutoff point designed for digital-based on our analysis of hundreds of modern cameras.’ The filter, which is housed inside a knurled brass frame, is also water, oil and scratch-resistant, thanks to three dozen layers of coatings Kolari Vision applies to the Gorilla Glass.</p>\n<table Windows 10 ARM devices. The release requires a Windows 10 ARM device running Windows 10 64-bit v190141.488.0 (Win10 20H1) and a minimum of 8GB of RAM, although 16GB is recommended. It is important to note that if you intend to install 32-bit applications from Adobe, you should not install the 64-bit version of Creative Cloud required for the new ARM-compatible Photoshop update.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/8800173072/photoshop-windows-arm-surface-pro-x-family.jpeg\" target=\"article-a35b1bca0efd4b00a2b581239be8ba10\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"190\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/8800173072/photoshop-windows-arm-surface-pro-x-family.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"photoshop-windows-arm-surface-pro-x-family.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/8800173072/photoshop-windows-arm-surface-pro-x-family.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">Microsoft Surface Pro X</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>As has been the case with native versions of Photoshop for Apple M1 machines, the first release of Photoshop for Windows ARM devices is not feature-complete. The omissions, which are fully outlined <a href=\"https://helpx.adobe.com/photoshop/kb/windows-arm-support.html\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">here</a>, are mostly minor and will be addressed in subsequent releases. Features unavailable in the native mode include working with embedded video layers, the Shake Reduction filter, Invite to Edit workflows, Windows Dial Support, opening U3D files, starting Photoshop using Lightroom's 'Edit In' command, Plugin Marketplace and more. There are also a variety of known issues that Adobe is working to address, including instability, freezing and issues with printing.</p> \n<p>Even with some issues and missing features, this is a major step forward for Adobe and finally answers the call of many Windows ARM users who have been wanting to use Photoshop on their devices. This week's release makes devices like Microsoft's Surface Pro X tablet a much more appealing option for photographers using Photoshop in their workflows.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/8800173072/photoshop-windows-arm-surface-pro-x-side-angle.jpeg\" target=\"article-a35b1bca0efd4b00a2b581239be8ba10\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"308\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/8800173072/photoshop-windows-arm-surface-pro-x-side-angle.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"photoshop-windows-arm-surface-pro-x-side-angle.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/8800173072/photoshop-windows-arm-surface-pro-x-side-angle.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">The Microsoft Surface Pro X is a much more appealing machine to photographers now that Adobe Photoshop is available on the device.</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Photoshop for Windows ARM devices has been a long time coming. 11th-generation processors, many new laptops are hitting the market, including the Razer Blade 15 refresh <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/news/9204931981/razer-announces-new-blade-15-with-4k-oled-touchscreen-rtx-graphics-faster-memory\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">we wrote about</a> earlier this week. Not to be left out, HP has <a href=\"https://press.hp.com/us/en/press-releases/2021/z-by-hp-powers-collaboration-everywhere.html\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">announced</a> new ZBook G8 laptops, only nine months after its ZBook Firefly models were announced. Updates are fast and furious these days. The new ZBook G8 range includes a trio of models, including 15.6\" and 17.3\" variants.</p> \n<p>The ZBook Studio and Power models come only in 15.6\" versions, while the Fury model is also available with a 17.3\" display. Displays come in Full HD and 4K flavors, including brightness up to 1,000 nits, which should be suitable for an HDR workflow. Processor options include Intel Zeon or 11th-gen H-series processors up to the Core i9 CPU. Storage is available up to a whopping 2TB.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0167808099/hp-zbook-g8-trio.jpeg\" target=\"article-21bd342ac08448cd96be5634a1534328\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"125\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/0167808099/hp-zbook-g8-trio.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"hp-zbook-g8-trio.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0167808099/hp-zbook-g8-trio.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">Left to right: ZBook Studio G8, ZBook Fury G8 and ZBook Power G8</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>There are a lot of options, and caveats, too. While a display with 1,000 nits of maximum brightness is available, that's only true of the 15.6\" model with a Full HD display. If you want 4K, the maximum brightness darkens to 600 nits (or 550 nits in the case of the 17.3\" display). The ZBook Studio has the most GPU options to choose from and is the only model in the new range to include Nvidia RTX 3060 to 3080 graphics cards. The ZBook Fury offers AMD Radeon Pro graphics instead. The maximum RAM varies among the different models, with the Fury offering up to 128GB RAM, whereas the Studio and Power models top out at 32GB and 64GB, respectively.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0167808099/hp-zbook-g8-1.jpeg\" target=\"article-21bd342ac08448cd96be5634a1534328\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"372\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/0167808099/hp-zbook-g8-1.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"hp-zbook-g8-1.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0167808099/hp-zbook-g8-1.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>There's a lot to keep track of, so let's refer to HP to learn more about the target audience for each model. HP says that the ZBook Studio G8 offers 'performance in a transformative size; designed for mobility – at home or on the road.' The ZBook Fury G8, on the other hand, goes all-out: 'Content creators get unthrottled performance and full expandability in a more portable design – desktop-level performance in a mobile form factor.' Rounding out the lineup is the entry-level option, the ZBook Power G8, which is 'HP's most affordable mobile workstation' and 'makes the power and pro certifications of a ZBook more accessible and ideal for STEAM students.'</p> \n<p>'Professional creators and power users need a curated, personalized software and hardware experience that aligns to the different ways they work and collaborate,' said Jim Nottingham, general manager and global head, Advanced Compute and Solutions, HP Inc. 'With the ZBook Studio being the most powerful workstation of its size, and the ZBook Fury offering full expandability in a portable design, HP is giving the professional community access to cutting-edge technology, unthrottled performance, and the versatility to make the next creative breakthrough a reality.'</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0167808099/hp-zbook-g8-studio-1.jpeg\" target=\"article-21bd342ac08448cd96be5634a1534328\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"495\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/0167808099/hp-zbook-g8-studio-1.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"hp-zbook-g8-studio-1.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0167808099/hp-zbook-g8-studio-1.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">The HP ZBook Studio G8 has a full RGB keyboard</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Looking closer at the HP ZBook G8 Studio, the notebook is designed to 'free the creative mind.' To that end, it's a purpose-built machine aimed to meet the demanding needs of creative applications and workflows. HP's DreamColor displays cover 100% of DCI-P3 and include Pantone validation. The Studio includes Nvidia RTZ A5000 or GeForce RTX 3080 laptop GPUs and 11th-gen Intel Core i9 vPro processors.</p> \n<p>The Fury is the world's most expandable 15\" and 17\" mobile workstation, per HP. The Fury packs desktop-class performance into a sleek, slim notebook design. The display is a next-gen DreamColor display with Pantone validation. The chassis is constructed using aluminum and includes tool-free expandability plus a wide array of ports, including Thunderbolt 4, HDMI, Mini DisplayPort, USB-A and more. With Intel Core i9 and Xeon processors, Nvidia RTX graphics, and up to 128GB of 3200MHz system memory, the Fury promises high-end performance.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0167808099/hp-zbook-g8-2.jpeg\" target=\"article-21bd342ac08448cd96be5634a1534328\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"331\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/0167808099/hp-zbook-g8-2.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"hp-zbook-g8-2.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0167808099/hp-zbook-g8-2.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\"> </td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>HP's most affordable mobile workstation, the ZBook Power, is all about delivering performance at lower prices. face-detection autofocus, an updated version of Adobe Lightroom and more. The best part is, firmware version 1.4 for the ZX1 is available to download directly to the camera over Wi-Fi.</p> \n<p>The first new feature Zeiss notes is face-detection autofocus, which works in both Single and Continuous AF shooting modes. While the ZX1 will detect faces on its own, you can also specify a face by tapping on the live view touchscreen display. Zeiss has also added full-res DNG rendering when viewing images in Gallery mode as well as an updated version of Adobe Lightroom (version 6.2).</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/8372392390/Zeiss_ZX1_Firmware_version_1.4_1.jpeg\" target=\"article-216d21eebb20446eada1625c3d788497\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"292\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/8372392390/Zeiss_ZX1_Firmware_version_1.4_1.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"Zeiss_ZX1_Firmware_version_1.4_1.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1040x0~articles/8372392390/Zeiss_ZX1_Firmware_version_1.4_1.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 520px;\">A screenshot of the face-detection AF mode as seen on the camera's liveview touchscreen.</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>The update also adds support for Zeiss’ ZX1 Companion App for Android and iOS, which enables remote control and liveview as well as photo geotagging using the GPS data from your mobile device. /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Photographer and self-professed weird lens guru <a href=\"https://www.mathieustern.com\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Mathieu Stern</a> is back with another interesting bit of photo gear. Unlike many of his videos, like <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/news/8412361503/video-capturing-video-and-portraits-with-a-canon-65mm-f0-75-x-ray-lens\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">this one about shooting with a Canon X-ray lens</a>, Stern's newest video is about a modern, commercially available product, the <a href=\"https://fotodioxpro.com/search?type=product&amp;q=+RhinoCam+Vertex\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Fotodiox RhinoCam Vertex Rotating Stitching Adapter</a>. The RhinoCam Vertex allows you to attach a medium format lens to a full-frame mirrorless camera, including Canon RF, Nikon Z and Sony E-mount cameras. Compatible lenses include Bronica ETR mount, Pentax 6x7 (P67), Pentax 645 (P645) and Hasselblad V-Mount.</p> \n<p>The RhinoCam Vertex rotates your camera on the lens to allow you to capture four different images, which can be used to stitch a 6x6 digital medium format image. The adapter takes advantage of the large image circle of a medium format lens relative to a full-frame image sensor. With a medium format lens attached to the RhinoCam Vertex and mounted on your camera, you then rotate the camera 360 degrees in 90-degree increments to capture four images around the center of the lens. Using digital stitching software, such as Photoshop, you then stitch the images into a panorama, replicating a medium format 'look' and resolution.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/4219454295/fotodiox-rhinocam-vertex.jpeg\" target=\"article-9a7171f0d4da470cac1f9789e5f68d9f\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"382\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/4219454295/fotodiox-rhinocam-vertex.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"fotodiox-rhinocam-vertex.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/4219454295/fotodiox-rhinocam-vertex.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Mathieu Stern went hands-on with the RhinoCam Vertex in his latest video. In his video, Stern used a Zenza Bronica Zenzanon-PE 75mm F2.8 lens on his Sony A7R III. Stern shows an overview of the adapter from Fotodiox, which is available in full further down, and shows some of his images. As you can tell, Stern is a big fan of the RhinoCam Vertex.</p> \n<div class=\"video\">\n <iframe allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"326\" id=\"videoFrame\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/swO3jnd6_TU?rel=0&amp;autohide=1&amp;wmode=transparent&amp;enablejsapi=1\" width=\"580\"></iframe>\n</div> \n<p>Fotodiox has published a couple of videos about the RhinoCam Vertex since releasing it earlier this year. The first video below is a general overview video of the product. By stitching together four full-frame images captured using a medium format lens, you can create an image with about 2.5 times the resolution of a standard full-frame image.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/4219454295/fotodiox-rhinocam-vertex-sample-image-1.jpeg\" target=\"article-9a7171f0d4da470cac1f9789e5f68d9f\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"590\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/4219454295/fotodiox-rhinocam-vertex-sample-image-1.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"fotodiox-rhinocam-vertex-sample-image-1.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/4219454295/fotodiox-rhinocam-vertex-sample-image-1.jpeg 2x\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">Using the Fotodiox RhinoCam Vertex, you rotate your camera 360 degrees to capture four full-frame images. You then stitch the images using an editing application like Photoshop to create a 6x6 digital medium format image. To minimize the need to reach across the screen when changing settings, Lux has included what it calls an ‘expandable honeycomb’ next to the shutter button that brings up the most commonly needed settings and tools</p>\n<p>Since iPads tend to be more two-handed devices, Lux has also added a feature that will 'flip' the interface so it's left-hand oriented for the southpaws out there.</p>\n<div id=\"embeddedSampleGallery_5947884917\" class=\"sampleGalleryImageViewerContainer\" style=\"height: 718px\"></div><script type=\"text/javascript\">$(document).ready(function() { SampleGalleryV2({\"containerId\":\"embeddedSampleGallery_5947884917\",\"galleryId\":\"5947884917\",\"isEmbeddedWidget\":true,\"selectedImageIndex\":0,\"isMobile\":false}) });</script>\n<p>Lux has also addressed the issue of the iPad’s unusual aspect ratio that can sometimes make for a confusing experience when shooting. It’s called ‘Pro View,’ and what it does is shrink the liveview display into the center of the screen so it’s easier to see the entire scene and compose a shot. Doing this also adds extra space on the display to more prominently display the histogram, waveform, manual focus and other pro features, ensuring nothing overlaps with the liveview. star-filled night sky at the ESA's Ariane 6 launch site in French Guiana, South America. Europe's Spaceport in French Guiana is preparing for the arrival of Ariane 6, 'Europe's next-generation launch vehicle.'</p>\n<div class=\"video\"><iframe allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"326\" id=\"videoFrame\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/3Cvd_zIOP_I?rel=0&amp;autohide=1&amp;wmode=transparent&amp;enablejsapi=1\" width=\"580\"></iframe></div>\n<p>The Ariana 6 rocket will come in two versions depending on mission requirements. The A62 has two strap-on boosters, while the A64 has four. The Ariane 6 is 207' (63m) tall with a diameter of 18' (5.4m). The mass of the rocket ranges from 1,170,000-1,900,000 lbs (530,000-860,000kg). Replacing the Ariane 6 launch vehicle, the Ariane 6's maiden test flight is scheduled for 2022 following several delays.</p>\n<p>You can see what a typical Ariane 6 mission might look like in the ESA's video below. Ariane 62 can launch payloads of approximately 9,920 lbs (4,500kg) into a geostationary orbit and 22,700 lbs (10,300kg) into low Earth orbit. By strapping on an additional two boosters, Ariane 64 can launch payloads of around 25,350 lbs (11,500kg) into geostationary orbit and 45,400 lbs (20,600kg) into low Earth orbit. With a full payload, Ariane 6 weighs about the same as one and a half Airbus A380 passenger airplanes.</p>\n<div class=\"video\"><iframe allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"326\" id=\"videoFrame\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/kcKL_qR1dXM?rel=0&amp;autohide=1&amp;wmode=transparent&amp;enablejsapi=1\" width=\"580\"></iframe></div>\n<p>The development of Ariane 6 has comprised an industrial network of more than 600 companies in 13 European countries, including 350 small- and medium-sized companies. The development is led by prime contractor ArianeGroup. The Ariane 6 launch facilities in French Guiana, seen in the time-lapse video above, are being prepared by France's space agency, CNES.</p>\n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\">\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td class=\"image\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/5096144062/ariane-6-artists-illustration.jpeg\" target=\"article-6cb2010508f649c6a2ed298abd06b8b7\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"590\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/5096144062/ariane-6-artists-illustration.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"ariane-6-artists-illustration.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/5096144062/ariane-6-artists-illustration.jpeg 2x\"></a></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td class=\"caption\">Artist's rendition of the two configurations of Ariane 6, the two-booster A62 and the four-booster A64. We've constantly been training the AI models, reviewing results, and comparing those results with other noise removal products out there today. It was no easy task,' says Dan Harlacher, VP of Product at ON1. 'We knew there was a high bar to clear to say this is the fastest and best product for removing image noise while giving photographers the best results.'</p>\n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\">\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/4942096527/on1-nonoise-ai-example-iso-16000.jpeg\" target=\"article-88bd292facfb4582b46c67f269a24963\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"403\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/4942096527/on1-nonoise-ai-example-iso-16000.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"on1-nonoise-ai-example-iso-16000.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/4942096527/on1-nonoise-ai-example-iso-16000.jpeg 2x\"></a></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">Before (left) and after (right) using NoNoise AI. Click to enlarge. Image credit: ON1</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<p>ON1 NoNoise AI offers fast live previews and includes an Auto mode that incorporates user preferences. The software integrates with existing workflows and supports the most common photo editors and file formats, including the ability to save DNG raw files to maintain the entire tonal and color range of your photos.</p>\n<p>In addition to AI-based noise reduction, other key features include:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Fast and easy-to-use controls:</strong> ON1 states that results can be viewed in 'only a fraction' of the time it takes competing apps to produce viewable results. 'There are also far fewer controls to adjust without the limitation of sacrificing sharpness to reduce image noise.'</li>\n<li><strong>AI-based demosaicing:</strong> When considering raw images, considerable noise is due to the demosaicing process of raw processing. This step is combined with noise reduction in ON1 NoNoise AI, resulting in better noise reduction while increasing detail and sharpness.</li>\n<li><strong>Compatibility:</strong> You can open raw photos from more than 800 cameras in ON1 NoNoise AI, including from Fujifilm cameras. You can save your images in DNG raw files.</li>\n<li><strong>Combine and mask:</strong> ON1 NoNoise AI includes the option to combine multiple renditions of a photo along with multiple photos as layers. You can use built-in masking tools to blend and combine them at varying levels of noise reduction and sharpening, allowing for local editing and fine-tuned control.</li>\n</ul>\n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\">\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/4942096527/on1-nonoise-ai-combine-and-auto.jpeg\" target=\"article-88bd292facfb4582b46c67f269a24963\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"482\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/4942096527/on1-nonoise-ai-combine-and-auto.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"on1-nonoise-ai-combine-and-auto.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/4942096527/on1-nonoise-ai-combine-and-auto.jpeg 2x\"></a></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">ON1 includes masking tools and a user-influenced Auto function. Click to enlarge. Image credit: ON1</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Auto button with user preferences:</strong> The Auto button in ON1 NoNoise AI analyzes a photo and determines the correct amount of noise reduction using AI models. Customer preference will also be considered, such as whether the user wants to maintain some grain in an image or not, for example.</li>\n<li><strong>Exclusive progressive sharpening:</strong> ON1's exclusive Progressive Sharpening algorithm is included in its new noise reduction software. This allows the software to enhance sharpness and details in a photo without introducing halos and artifacts.</li>\n</ul>\n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\">\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/4942096527/on1-nonoise-ai-progressive-sharpening.jpeg\" target=\"article-4942096527\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"174\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/4942096527/on1-nonoise-ai-progressive-sharpening.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"on1-nonoise-ai-progressive-sharpening.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/4942096527/on1-nonoise-ai-progressive-sharpening.jpeg 2x\"></a></td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Presets:</strong> Users can create their own presets, and the software comes with some presets to help you get started.</li>\n<li><strong>Batch processing:</strong> You can batch process an entire folder of images in ON1 NoNoise AI. For each image in a batch, the 'correct amount of noise reduction and sharpening can be added.' You can also copy and paste settings from one photo to another.</li>\n<li><strong>Plug-in support:</strong> ON NoNoise AI works as a standalone application and as a plug-in for Adobe Photoshop, Adobe Lightroom Classic, Capture One, Affinity Photo, Corel Paint Shop Pro and Apple Photos.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>'Our dedicated AI team is hitting their stride with this release. Last fall, Portrait AI was the team's first AI-based product release, which has been a huge success. From the start, we didn't want to build an AI-based product just because AI is the new trend in software development,' says Craig Keudell, President of ON1. 'The team realizes the potential benefits of implementing AI methodologies in photo editing applications. When AI is done right, it can be a beneficial technology from the photographer. AI can greatly simplify the editing process for the photographer while creating amazing images.'</p>\n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\">\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/4942096527/on1-nonoise-ai-ui-plugins.jpeg\" target=\"article-88bd292facfb4582b46c67f269a24963\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"331\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/4942096527/on1-nonoise-ai-ui-plugins.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"on1-nonoise-ai-ui-plugins.jpeg\" srcset=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/4942096527/on1-nonoise-ai-ui-plugins.jpeg 2x\"></a></td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<p>ON1 NoNoise AI will be available in the second half of June.
